And neither do we unless you supply meaningful information. Start by posting the output from ```
top
``` Just the first 10 lines will suffice. Please post all data in between code tags.

### Post by Gnusboy on 2014-08-07
[B]
I apologize for all the garbage post in my question. It's just one of the problems I'm having right now![/B] 

 
I have no idea what's happening to my system.
It suddenly began using nearly 100% of system load causing system hang and monitor gray out for many seconds. This happened over and over and it has not happened before.
I'm using Ubuntu 12.04
AMD quad core
4 GB ram
640 HDD

At the time this started I was browsing with Firefox with 8 tabs open. It started slowing down and hanging for no apparent reason.
I was able to open the system monitor and it suddenly started using 100% of resources then it would return to normal. It was also showing 2.2 GB or memory use
As I type this it's doing the same thing. It freezes, then returns to normal.
I have made no changes to the OS, and lately used just Firefox and Libre Office.
A few days ago the Update Manager started showing 50 new updates - but they were listed as KDE security changes.
[B]I have never installed KDE on my system.

[/B]Some of the installed Ubuntu tools are now showing as KDE applications - not Ubuntu
NetworkManager
I've used UBUNTU 12.04 only since it's original install. I asked about this on the Forum and was told I should go ahead and install these up dates
and that they would not conflict with my current system. I wanted to learn more so I did not install any of these updates.
Today, the Update Manager lists a total of 59 Updates waiting to be installed.

Here is a screenshot of the system monitor data:


If anyone can help figure this out I will appreciate the help. Thanks

### Post by mariskaoldtina on 2014-08-07
> **Gnusboy said:**
>  I don't know what you're asking for with "Top"

1) Open a terminal
2) type in "top"
3) hit ENTER

it will display what is going on.

### Post by whitesmith on 2014-08-07
> **Gnusboy said:**
> Whitesmith
Which code do you mean? I don't know what you're asking for with "Top"

I apologize for all the extraneous posts. Everything was freezing and I was not getting confirmations.

Top is a shell command. Open a GUI Terminal by typing Ctrl+Alt+t In that terminal type```
top -bn1
```. When the display goes back to the command line (your home directory, probably), scroll to the top of the window and copy the first 10 or 12 lines. These are the 10 or 12 processes that are sucking the life out of your system. Paste the block of data you copied between code tags and post it so that we can see it. I'll have a peek in the morning. Regards.

---

### Post by CantankRus on 2014-08-07
Check your mem and swap usage in terminal and post your output. Enter  **free -m**
```
@Trusty:~$ **free -m**
             total       used       free     shared    buffers     cached
Mem:          3935       2512       1422         39        256       1017
-/+ buffers/cache:       1239       2695
Swap:            0          0          0

```

---

### Post by Rob Sayer on 2014-08-08
You don't have to have the KDE desktop installed to get a lot of KDE updates.  All you need is to have installed programs(s) from the KDE desktop libraries.  KDE is a highly integrated DE so installing almost any KDE apps will also install a lot of dependencies.

This is not really a problem, and I doubt very much it was causing your issues.  I use dolphin as my default file manager in whatever other DE I'm going to use.  It's so powerful and configurable I don't want anything else.  And it did install a lot of dependencies, but they don't run if dolphin doesn't need them.

---

### Post by whitesmith on 2014-08-08
Hello again. Your posted figures look normal to my eyes. Since things returned to normal after installing the 59 upgrades, I'm tempted to speculate that one solved your problem. Firefox misbehavior is another possibility. Those are not scientific statements, just SWAGS, because there's no way to disprove any of them.

After installing a large number of updates I run these commands, in order, just to make sure that my machine is running properly:```
sudo apt-get update
``` and then:```
sudo apt-get upgrade
``` and then:```
sudo apt-get check
``` Unmet dependencies are fixed with:```
sudo apt-get -f install
``` You can read more about these commands in [https://help.ubuntu.com/community/AptGet/Howto](https://help.ubuntu.com/community/AptGet/Howto). I hope this procedure proves to be of help. Regards.

---
